            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>"Solid defense" still doesn't have much relevance in fantasy, right? Then neither does Tim Federowicz. The backstop rode the Triple-A train a few times in 2013, but eventually settled in as the primary backup to starter A.J. Ellis while hitting only .231/.275/.356 in 173 plate appearances. In the minors, he'd shown a little bit more pop, but not as much as you'd think; his ridiculous Triple-A line in 2013 was in no small part due to the effects of the Pacific Coast League and Albuquerque in particular. Federowicz has a reputation for being a plus defensive catcher, and that will keep him in the big leagues, but his bat will prevent him from being a star -- and, perhaps, even more than a backup. <a href="http://www.twitter.com/mike_petriello">(Mike Petriello)</a><br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>There's plenty of good catchers who aren't very likely to hit at a big league level. Absolutely none of them belong on your fantasy team, Tim Federowicz included.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>The Los Angeles Dodgers packaged 27-year-old backup catcher Tim Federowicz alongside Matt Kemp in a deal with the San Diego Padres this offseason that returned catcher Yasmani Grandal and two pitching prospects. Considered by some to be more of a defensive specialist than a crafty batsman, Federowicz will likely be in a similar backup, platoon, or late-inning defensive replacement situation in San Diego with newly acquired backstop Derek Norris earning most of the plate appearances as the Friars’ primary backstop. In seven years on the farm, Federowicz compiled a .293/.359/.465 slash line with a sprinkle of pop (65 home runs and 352 runs batted in), so the ability to make contact and get on base is there. But in just 89 games in the first division, the right-hander owns an ugly .194/.247/.300 triple slash with five long balls, 22 RBI and an awful 29.5% strikeout rate. In deeper “only” leagues that roster two catchers, Federowicz could be an option for owners simply looking to gather plate appearances. (<a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/%E2%80%9Dhttp://www.twitter.com/thefantasyfix%E2%80%9D">Alan Harrison</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Federowicz is more of a defensive specialist than run producer, so he'll likely be in a backup, platoon or late-inning defensive replacement situation in San Diego. He should only be considered for owners in super deep two catcher formats.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        
        
    </tr>
